{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01JcHXgP2MuJFHtX9j1T5tXf","type":"tool_result","content":"## Sinks\n\nTelemetry events are dispatched to one or more sinks. Sinks are configured independently.\n\n### File Sink (default, always on)\n\nWrites JSONL to per-worker log files:\n\n```\n~/.needle/logs/<worker-id>.jsonl\n```\n\n- One line per event\n- File is append-only\n- Rotation: new file per session (session ID in filename) or size-based (configurable)\n\n### Stdout Sink (optional)\n\nWrites human-readable summary to stdout for interactive monitoring:\n\n```\n15:30:00 [alpha] CLAIMED nd-a3f8 (p1: \"Fix auth middleware\")\n15:30:02 [alpha] DISPATCHED claude-sonnet pid=12345\n15:32:15 [alpha] SUCCESS nd-a3f8 (135s, ~2400 tokens)\n15:32:15 [alpha] CLAIMED nd-b2c9 (p2: \"Add rate limiting tests\")\n```\n\n- Enabled when worker runs in foreground or via `needle attach`\n- Format is configurable: `minimal`, `normal`, `verbose`\n- Color-coded by event type\n\n### Hook Sink (optional)\n\nDispatches events to external systems via webhook or command:\n\n```yaml\ntelemetry:\n  hooks:\n    - event_filter: \"outcome.*\"\n      command: \"curl -X POST https://webhook.example.com/needle -d @-\"\n    - event_filter: \"worker.errored\"\n      command: \"/path/to/alert-script.sh\"\n    - event_filter: \"effort.recorded\"\n      command: \"/path/to/cost-tracker.sh\"\n```\n\n- Events matching the filter are piped as JSON to the command's stdin\n- Hook execution is fire-and-forget (non-blocking)\n- Failed hooks emit a `telemetry.hook.failed` event to the file sink (not recursively to hooks)\n\n### OTLP Sink (optional)\n\nExports telemetry as OpenTelemetry signals (traces, metrics, logs) over OTLP to any compliant collector (OpenTelemetry Collector, Jaeger, Tempo, Grafana Alloy, Honeycomb, Datadog, etc.). This is the canonical integration point for FABRIC and any downstream observability plane.\n\n```yaml\ntelemetry:\n  otlp:\n    enabled: true\n    endpoint: \"http://otel-collector.tailnet:4317\"    # gRPC default; use 4318 for HTTP\n    protocol: grpc                                     # grpc | http/protobuf\n    headers:\n      authorization: \"Bearer ${OTEL_TOKEN}\"            # env interpolation\n    timeout_ms: 5000\n    compression: gzip                                  # none | gzip\n    tls:\n      insecure: false\n      ca_file: \"\"\n    signals:\n      traces: true\n      metrics: true\n      logs: true\n    resource_attributes:\n      deployment.environment: \"production\"\n      service.namespace: \"needle-fleet\"\n```\n\nDesign:\n\n- **Non-blocking.** Uses a batch span/log/metric processor. If the collector is unreachable, events are buffered up to a bounded queue, then dropped (same policy as file sink). Drops emit a `telemetry.otlp.dropped` event to the file sink (never recursively to OTLP).\n- **Additive.** The file sink is authoritative. OTLP is an export, not a replacement. If OTLP is disabled or misconfigured, NEEDLE behaves identically to a file-sink-only deployment.\n- **Stdlib deps.** Rust crates: `opentelemetry`, `opentelemetry_sdk`, `opentelemetry-otlp`, `opentelemetry-semantic-conventions`. All support OTLP/gRPC and OTLP/HTTP.\n- **W3C trace context.** Trace and span IDs are generated per the W3C Trace Context spec so they interop with any OTel backend.\n- **Graceful shutdown.** On `worker.stopped`, the exporter is flushed with a deadline before process exit. Failure to flush is logged but never blocks shutdown.\n\n## OpenTelemetry Semantic Mapping\n\nNEEDLE's existing event catalog maps cleanly to OpenTelemetry's three signal types. This mapping is **normative** — the OTLP sink implementation must conform to it so dashboards and alerts remain stable across NEEDLE versions.\n\n### Resource Attributes\n\nEvery exported signal carries these resource attributes (per OTel semantic conventions):\n\n| Attribute | Value | Source |\n|-----------|-------|--------|\n| `service.name` | `\"needle\"` | Constant |\n| `service.version` | build version | `env!(\"CARGO_PKG_VERSION\")` |\n| `service.instance.id` | `<worker_id>` | e.g., `needle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha` |\n| `service.namespace` | `\"needle-fleet\"` (default, configurable) | Config |\n| `deployment.environment` | e.g., `\"production\"` | Config |\n| `host.name` | hostname | OS |\n| `process.pid` | worker PID | OS |\n| `needle.agent` | e.g., `\"claude-anthropic-sonnet\"` | Worker config |\n| `needle.model` | e.g., `\"claude-sonnet-4-6\"` | Worker config |\n| `needle.session_id` | session ID | Per-boot random |\n| `needle.workspace` | workspace path | Worker config |\n\n### Traces\n\nThe NEEDLE state machine is naturally hierarchical, which maps directly to OTel spans.\n\n```\nworker.session                                          (root span, lifetime = worker process)\n├── strand.pluck                                        (one per strand evaluation)\n│   └── bead.lifecycle                                  (one per claimed bead)\n│       ├── bead.claim                                  (ATOMIC phase)\n│       ├── bead.prompt_build\n│       ├── agent.dispatch                              (DISPATCHING + EXECUTING)\n│       │   └── agent.execution                         (process alive; span.ok on exit 0)\n│       └── bead.outcome                                (HANDLING)\n│           └── bead.mitosis?                           (optional, if outcome = failure)\n├── strand.mend\n├── strand.explore\n├── strand.weave\n├── strand.unravel\n├── strand.pulse\n└── strand.knot                                         (terminal backoff / exhaustion)\n```\n\nSpan naming follows OpenTelemetry conventions: lowercase dotted, verb-form where appropriate.\n\n**Span attributes** follow OTel semantic conventions where applicable, plus a `needle.*` namespace:\n\n| Span | Key Attributes |\n|------|----------------|\n| `worker.session` | `needle.beads_processed`, `needle.uptime_seconds`, `needle.exit_reason` |\n| `strand.*` | `needle.strand.name`, `needle.strand.result`, `needle.strand.duration_ms` |\n| `bead.lifecycle` | `needle.bead.id`, `needle.bead.priority`, `needle.bead.title_hash`, `needle.bead.outcome` |\n| `bead.claim` | `needle.claim.retry_number`, `needle.claim.result` (`succeeded` / `race_lost` / `failed`) |\n| `agent.dispatch` | `gen_ai.system` (e.g., `anthropic`), `gen_ai.request.model`, `gen_ai.usage.input_tokens`, `gen_ai.usage.output_tokens`, `needle.agent.pid`, `needle.agent.exit_code` |\n| `bead.outcome` | `needle.outcome` (`success` / `failure` / `timeout` / `crash` / `agent_not_found` / `interrupted`), `needle.outcome.action` |\n\n**GenAI semantic conventions.** The `agent.dispatch` span uses OTel's `gen_ai.*` conventions so NEEDLE's token/cost data shows up in GenAI dashboards out-of-the-box (Grafana GenAI app, Langfuse, Honeycomb AI, etc.).\n\n**Span status.** Success outcomes set `Status::Ok`. All other outcomes set `Status::Error` with a description matching the `needle.outcome` value. This makes error-rate SLOs trivial.\n\n**Context propagation.** The trace ID from `worker.session` is recorded in the file-sink event envelope as a new optional field `trace_id`, enabling correlation between the JSONL file sink and the OTel backend without ambiguity.\n\n### Metrics\n\nMetrics are emitted via the OTel Meter API, one `Meter` per worker. All metrics are prefixed `needle.*`.\n\n| Metric | Instrument | Unit | Attributes | Description |\n|--------|-----------|------|------------|-------------|\n| `needle.workers.active` | UpDownCounter | `{worker}` | — | Current live worker count (incremented on `worker.started`, decremented on `worker.stopped`) |\n| `needle.beads.claimed` | Counter | `{bead}` | `strand`, `priority` | Successful bead claims |\n| `needle.beads.completed` | Counter | `{bead}` | `outcome` | Bead terminal outcomes (one per `bead.outcome`) |\n| `needle.beads.duration` | Histogram | `ms` | `outcome` | End-to-end bead lifecycle time |\n| `needle.claim.attempts` | Counter | `{attempt}` | `result` (`succeeded`/`race_lost`/`failed`) | Claim attempts |\n| `needle.strand.duration` | Histogram | `ms` | `strand`, `result` | Strand evaluation time |\n| `needle.agent.duration` | Histogram | `ms` | `agent`, `model`, `exit_code` | Agent process runtime |\n| `needle.agent.tokens.input` | Counter | `{token}` | `agent`, `model` | Input tokens consumed |\n| `needle.agent.tokens.output` | Counter | `{token}` | `agent`, `model` | Output tokens produced |\n| `needle.cost.usd` | Counter | `USD` | `agent`, `model` | Estimated cost accumulator |\n| `needle.heartbeat.age` | Gauge (observable) | `s` | `worker_id` | Seconds since last heartbeat emitted by this worker |\n| `needle.peers.stale` | UpDownCounter | `{peer}` | — | Currently-stale peers observed by this worker |\n| `needle.queue.depth` | Gauge (observable) | `{bead}` | `workspace`, `priority` | Open beads visible to this worker (sampled at strand evaluation) |\n| `needle.mitosis.children_created` | Counter | `{bead}` | `parent_id` | Mitosis child creations |\n| `needle.outcome.rate` | derived | — | — | Computed in the backend as `needle.beads.completed{outcome=\"success\"} / needle.beads.completed` |\n\nMetric aggregation temporality is **delta** (standard OTel default); backends that require cumulative (Prometheus via prometheusreceiver) convert upstream.\n\n### Logs\n\nEvery NEEDLE telemetry event that isn't already represented as a span event is exported as an OTel LogRecord with:\n\n- `severity_number` / `severity_text`: `INFO` for normal events, `WARN` for `peer.stale` / `telemetry.*.dropped`, `ERROR` for `worker.errored` / `bead.claim.failed` / `agent.timeout`.\n- `body`: the existing event `data` object.\n- `attributes`: flattened from the event envelope (`event_type`, `bead_id`, `workspace`, etc.).\n- `trace_id` / `span_id`: linked to the enclosing `bead.lifecycle` or `worker.session` span where applicable.\n\nEvents that ARE spans (e.g., `bead.claim.attempted` → a span, not a log) do not double-export as logs.\n\n### Span Events vs. Logs\n\nIntra-span state changes (e.g., `agent.executing` heartbeats, `heartbeat.emitted`) are recorded as OTel **span events** on the nearest enclosing span, not as separate logs. This keeps the signal count manageable and makes timelines in Tempo/Jaeger readable.","is_error":false}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VbCthM7zZQgJ89evLxCytY","session_id":"59f8ae06-af96-473c-97e9-6017642d50f8","uuid":"b9bcec2b-d5e5-4939-9f78-5ab3f0a6189a","timestamp":"2026-04-21T12:28:08.926Z"}

TelemetrySink Trait (lines 1091-1102)\n\n```rust\npub trait TelemetrySink: Send + Sync {\n    fn write(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> Result<()>;\n    fn flush(&self) -> Result<()>;\n}\n```\n\n**Three built-in implementations:**\n\n#### **FileSink** (lines 1104-1169)\n- Writes JSONL to `~/.needle/logs/<worker-id>-<session-id>.jsonl`\n- Append-only, one event per line\n- BufWriter for efficiency\n- Mutex-protected for thread safety\n- Methods: `new()`, `with_dir()`, `path()`\n\n#### **StdoutSink** (lines 1171-1423)\n- Human-readable format for interactive monitoring\n- Configurable verbosity: Minimal, Normal, Verbose\n- Color-coded by event type (red for errors, green for success, etc.)\n- Format: `HH:MM:SS [worker] EVENT bead_id summary`\n- ANSI color codes based on event category\n- Auto-detects TTY for color (via libc `isatty`)\n- Methods: `new()`, `format_event()`, `event_summary()`, `short_type()`, `colorize()`\n\n#### **HookSink** (lines 1446-1616)\n- Dispatches matching events to external systems (fire-and-forget)\n- Supports glob-pattern event filters\n- Two dispatch modes per hook:\n  - **Command**: Shell execution with JSON piped to stdin\n  - **URL**: HTTP POST with Content-Type: application/json\n- 10-second timeout for HTTP requests\n- Failed hooks emit `telemetry.sink_error` events (not recursively)\n- Methods: `new()`, `is_empty()`, `dispatch()`, `run_hook()`, `post_url()`\n- Regex-based filter compilation from glob patterns\n\n---\n\n### 4. Telemetry Emitter (lines 1618-1988)\n\n**Non-blocking async architecture:**\n```\nworker → emit() → mpsc::Sender → [background task] → TelemetrySink(s)\n```\n\n#### **Telemetry struct** (lines 1628-1640)\n- `worker_id`: WorkerId\n- `session_id`: 8-char hex string\n- `sequence`: Arc<AtomicU64> (monotonic counter)\n- `sender`: Arc<Mutex<Option<mpsc::UnboundedSender>>>\n- `pending_writer`: Holds receiver + sinks until spawned\n- `writer_handle`: JoinHandle for background task\n\n#### **Factory Methods:**\n1. `new(worker_id)` - File sink only\n2. `with_stdout(worker_id, config)` - File + stdout\n3. `with_hooks(worker_id, stdout_config, hook_configs)` - File + stdout + hooks\n4. `from_config(worker_id, config)` - Selects based on config\n5. `with_log_dir(worker_id, log_dir)` - Custom log directory\n6. `with_log_dir_and_path()` - Testing variant (fixed session ID)\n7. `with_sink(worker_id, sink)` - Testing with custom sink\n\n#### **Core Methods:**\n- `emit(EventKind)` - Non-blocking, returns immediately, never panics\n- `start()` - Spawns background writer task (must be in tokio context)\n- `shutdown()` - Flushes all sinks, awaits completion\n- `session_id()`, `worker_id()` - Accessors\n\n#### **Background Writer** (lines 1948-1987)\nSpawned as tokio::spawn, continuously:\n1. Receives events from mpsc channel\n2. Writes to file sink (if present)\n3. Writes to stdout sink (if present)\n4. Dispatches to hooks (if present), captures failures\n5. Writes hook failures to file sink only\n6. On channel close: flushes all sinks and exits\n\n---\n\n### 5. };\n                let dur = event\n                    .duration_ms\n                    .map(|d| format!(\" {}ms\", d))\n                    .unwrap_or_default();\n                let line =      self.colorize(etype, &line)\n                } else {\n                    line\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Shorten the dotted event type to an uppercase action word.\n    fn short_type(event_type: &str) -> &str {\n        match event_type {\n            \"worker.started\" => \"STARTED\",\n            \"worker.stopped\" => \"STOPPED\",\n            \"worker.errored\" => \"ERROR\",\n            \"worker.exhausted\" => \"EXHAUSTED\",\n            \"worker.idle\" => \"IDLE\",\n            \"worker.state_transition\" => \"STATE\",\n            \"worker.queue_empty\" => \"QUEUE_EMPTY\",\n            \"strand.evaluated\" => \"STRAND\",\n            \"strand.skipped\" => \"STRAND_SKIP\",\n            \"bead.claim.attempted\" => \"CLAIMING\",\n            \"bead.claim.succeeded\" => \"CLAIMED\",\n            \"bead.claim.race_lost\" => \"RACE_LOST\",\n            \"bead.claim.failed\" => \"CLAIM_FAIL\",\n            \"bead.released\" => \"RELEASED\",\n            \"bead.completed\" => \"COMPLETED\",\n            \"bead.orphaned\" => \"ORPHANED\",\n            \"agent.dispatched\" => \"DISPATCHED\",\n            \"agent.completed\" => \"AGENT_DONE\",\n            \"outcome.classified\" => \"OUTCOME\",\n            \"outcome.handled\" => \"HANDLED\",\n            \"heartbeat.emitted\" => \"HEARTBEAT\",\n            \"peer.stale\" => \"PEER_STALE\",\n            \"peer.crashed\" => \"PEER_CRASHED\",\n            \"health.check\" => \"HEALTH\",\n            \"effort.recorded\" => \"EFFORT\",\n            \"budget.warning\" => \"BUDGET_WARN\",\n            \"budget.stop\" => \"BUDGET_STOP\",\n            \"rate_limit.wait\" => \"RATE_WAIT\",\n            \"rate_limit.allowed\" => \"RATE_OK\",\n            \"bead.mitosis.evaluated\" => \"MITOSIS_EVAL\",\n            \"bead.mitosis.split\" => \"MITOSIS\",\n            \"bead.mitosis.skipped\" => \"MITOSIS_SKIP\",\n            \"mend.orphaned_lock_removed\" => \"MEND_LOCK\",\n            \"mend.dependency_cleaned\" => \"MEND_DEP\",\n            \"mend.db_repaired\" => \"MEND_REPAIR\",\n            \"mend.db_rebuilt\" => \"MEND_REBUILD\",\n            \"mend.cycle_summary\" => \"MEND_DONE\",\n            \"telemetry.sink_error\" => \"SINK_ERR\",\n            other => other,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Produce a brief summary from the event data.\n    fn event_summary(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> String {\n        let d = &event.data;\n        match event.event_type.as_str() {\n            \"bead.claim.succeeded\" => String::new(),\n            \"agent.dispatched\" => d[\"agent\"]\n                .as_str()\n                .map(|a| format!(\"agent={a}\"))\n                .unwrap_or_default(),\n            \"agent.completed\" => {\n                let exit = d[\"exit_code\"].as_i64().unwrap_or(-1);\n                let dur = d[\"duration_ms\"].as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n                format!(\"exit={exit}, {}\", format_duration_ms(dur))\n            }\n            \"outcome.classified\" => d[\"outcome\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"unknown\").to_string(),\n            \"outcome.handled\" => {\n                let outcome = d[\"outcome\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"?\");\n                let action = d[\"action\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"?\");\n                format!(\"{outcome} → {action}\")\n            }\n            \"effort.recorded\" => {\n                let agent = d[\"agent_name\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"?\");\n                let cost = d[\"estimated_cost_usd\"].as_f64();\n                let dur = d[\"elapsed_ms\"].as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n                match cost {\n                    Some(c) => format!(\"{agent}, {}, ${c:.4}\", format_duration_ms(dur)),\n                    None => format!(\"{agent}, {}\", format_duration_ms(dur)),\n                }\n            }\n            \"worker.stopped\" => {\n                let reason = d[\"reason\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"?\");\n                let beads = d[\"beads_processed\"].as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n                format!(\"{reason}, {beads} beads\")\n            }\n            \"worker.errored\" => d[\"error_message\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"unknown\").to_string(),\n            \"worker.idle\" => {\n                let secs = d[\"backoff_seconds\"].as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n                format!(\"backoff {secs}s\")\n            }\n            \"bead.mitosis.split\" => {\n                let created = d[\"children_created\"].as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n                format!(\"{created} children\")\n            }\n            \"budget.warning\" | \"budget.stop\" => {\n                let cost = d[\"daily_cost\"].as_f64().unwrap_or(0.0);\n                let thresh = d[\"threshold\"].as_f64().unwrap_or(0.0);\n                format!(\"${cost:.2}/${thresh:.2}\")\n            }\n            _ => String::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Wrap text in ANSI color based on event type category.\n    fn colorize(&self, event_type: &str, text: &str) -> String {\n        let code = match event_type {\n            t if t.starts_with(\"worker.errored\") || t.starts_with(\"budget.stop\") => \"\\x1b[31m\", // red\n            t if t.starts_with(\"bead.claim.succeeded\") || t == \"bead.completed\" => \"\\x1b[32m\", // green\n            t if t.starts_with(\"agent.\") || t.starts_with(\"outcome.\") => \"\\x1b[36m\", // cyan\n            t if t.starts_with(\"bead.claim.race_lost\")\n                || t.starts_with(\"bead.claim.failed\")\n                || t == \"bead.released\"\n                || t == \"bead.orphaned\" =>\n            {\n                \"\\x1b[33m\"\n            } // yellow\n            t if t.starts_with(\"budget.warning\") || t.starts_with(\"rate_limit\") => \"\\x1b[33m\", // yellow\n            t if t.starts_with(\"mend.\") || t.starts_with(\"peer.\") => \"\\x1b[35m\", // magenta\n            t if t.starts_with(\"heartbeat\") || t.starts_with(\"health\") => \"\\x1b[90m\", // dim\n            _ => \"\\x1b[0m\",                                                      // reset / default\n        };\n        format!(\"{code}{text}\\x1b[0m\")\n    }\n}\n\nimpl TelemetrySink for StdoutSink {\n    fn write(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> Result<()> {\n        let line = self.format_event(event);\n        println!(\"{line}\");\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    fn flush(&self) -> Result<()> {\n        use std::io::Write;\n        std::io::stdout().flush()?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Check if stdout is a terminal (for auto color detection).\nfn atty_stdout() -> bool {\n    unsafe { libc_isatty(1) != 0 }\n}\n\nextern \"C\" {\n    #[link_name = \"isatty\"]\n    fn libc_isatty(fd: i32) -> i32;\n}\n\n/// Public wrapper for formatting milliseconds as human-readable duration.\npub fn format_duration_ms_public(ms: u64) -> String {\n    format_duration_ms(ms)\n}\n\n/// Format milliseconds as human-readable duration.\nfn format_duration_ms(ms: u64) -> String {\n    if ms < 1000 {\n        format!(\"{ms}ms\")\n    } else if ms < 60_000 {\n        format!(\"{:.1}s\", ms as f64 / 1000.0)\n    } else {\n        let mins = ms / 60_000;\n        let secs = (ms % 60_000) / 1000;\n        format!(\"{mins}m{secs}s\")\n    }\n}\n\n// ─── Session ID generation ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\n/// Generate an 8-hex-char session ID.\n///\n/// Uses `/dev/urandom` when available, falls back to PID XOR timestamp.\npub fn generate_session_id() -> String {\n    // Try /dev/urandom (Linux/macOS)\n    if let Ok(mut f) = std::fs::File::open(\"/dev/urandom\") {\n        use std::io::Read;\n        let mut buf = [0u8; 4];\n        if f.read_exact(&mut buf).is_ok() {\n            return format!(\"{:02x}{:02x}{:02x}{:02x}\", buf[0], buf[1], buf[2], buf[3]);\n        }\n    }\n    // Fallback: PID XOR nanosecond timestamp\n    let pid = std::process::id();\n    let ts = Utc::now().timestamp_millis() as u64;\n    let hash = pid as u64 ^ ts;\n    format!(\"{:08x}\", hash & 0xffff_ffff)\n}\n\n// ─── HookSink ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\n/// A compiled hook: a pre-compiled regex filter + dispatch target(s).\nstruct CompiledHook {\n    filter: regex::Regex,\n    /// Shell command (empty = disabled).\n    command: String,\n    /// Webhook URL (None = disabled).\n    url: Option<String>,\n}\n\n/// Dispatches matching telemetry events to external commands and/or URLs.\n///\n/// Each hook has a glob pattern matched against `event_type`. When an event\n/// matches, the event JSON is piped to `command`'s stdin and/or HTTP-POSTed\n/// to `url`. Execution is fire-and-forget — failed hooks emit `SinkError`\n/// events to the file sink but never block the worker or recurse into hooks.\npub struct HookSink {\n    hooks: Vec<CompiledHook>,\n}\n\nimpl HookSink {\n    /// Compile hook configs into a `HookSink`.\n    ///\n    /// Returns an error if any `event_filter` is an invalid glob pattern.\n    pub fn new(configs: &[crate::config::HookConfig]) -> Result<Self> {\n        let mut hooks = Vec::with_capacity(configs.len());\n        for cfg in configs {\n            let filter = glob_to_regex(&cfg.event_filter)\n                .with_context(|| format!(\"invalid hook filter: {}\", cfg.event_filter))?;\n            hooks.push(CompiledHook {\n                filter,\n                command: cfg.command.clone(),\n                url: cfg.url.clone(),\n            });\n        }\n        Ok(HookSink { hooks })\n    }\n\n    /// Check whether any hooks are configured.\n    pub fn is_empty(&self) -> bool {\n        self.hooks.is_empty()\n    }\n\n    /// Dispatch an event to all matching hooks (fire-and-forget).\n    ///\n    /// Returns a list of `SinkError` events for hooks that failed, so the\n    /// caller can write them to the file sink without recursion.\n    pub fn dispatch(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> Vec<TelemetryEvent> {\n        // Never dispatch SinkError events to hooks — prevents recursion.\n        if event.event_type == \"telemetry.sink_error\" {\n            return Vec::new();\n        }\n\n        let json = match serde_json::to_string(event) {\n            Ok(j) => j,\n            Err(_) => return Vec::new(),\n        };\n\n        let mut failures = Vec::new();\n        for hook in &self.hooks {\n            if !hook.filter.is_match(&event.event_type) {\n                continue;\n            }\n\n            // Dispatch to command if configured.\n            if !hook.command.is_empty() {\n                match Self::run_hook(&hook.command, &json) {\n                    Ok(()) => {}\n                    Err(e) => {\n                        failures.push(TelemetryEvent {\n                            timestamp: Utc::now(),\n                            event_type: \"telemetry.sink_error\".to_string(),\n                            worker_id: event.worker_id.clone(),\n                            session_id: event.session_id.clone(),\n                            sequence: 0, // sequence is set by the emitter, not here\n                            bead_id: None,\n                            workspace: None,\n                            data: serde_json::json!({\n                                \"hook_command\": hook.command,\n                                \"event_filter\": hook.filter.as_str(),\n                                \"original_event_type\": event.event_type,\n                                \"error\": e.to_string(),\n                            }),\n                            duration_ms: None,\n                        });\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n\n            // Dispatch to URL if configured.\n            if let Some(ref url) = hook.url {\n                match Self::post_url(url, &json) {\n                    Ok(()) => {}\n                    Err(e) => {\n                        failures.push(TelemetryEvent {\n                            timestamp: Utc::now(),\n                            event_type: \"telemetry.sink_error\".to_string(),\n                            worker_id: event.worker_id.clone(),\n                            session_id: event.session_id.clone(),\n                            sequence: 0,\n                            bead_id: None,\n                            workspace: None,\n                            data: serde_json::json!({\n                                \"hook_url\": url,\n                                \"event_filter\": hook.filter.as_str(),\n                                \"original_event_type\": event.event_type,\n                                \"error\": e.to_string(),\n                            }),\n                            duration_ms: None,\n                        });\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        failures\n    }\n\n    /// Execute a single hook command, piping JSON to its stdin.\n    ///\n    /// Spawns `sh -c <command>` with the event JSON on stdin, waits for\n    /// completion, and returns an error if the command exits non-zero.\n    /// This runs inside the background writer task so blocking is acceptable.\n    fn run_hook(command: &str, json: &str) -> Result<()> {\n        use std::io::Write;\n        use std::process::{Command, Stdio};\n\n        let mut child = Command::new(\"sh\")\n            .arg(\"-c\")\n            .arg(command)\n            .stdin(Stdio::piped())\n            .stdout(Stdio::null())\n            .stderr(Stdio::null())\n            .spawn()\n            .with_context(|| format!(\"failed to spawn hook: {command}\"))?;\n\n        if let Some(mut stdin) = child.stdin.take() {\n            // Best-effort write; ignore broken pipe if child exits early.\n            let _ = stdin.write_all(json.as_bytes());\n        }\n\n        // Wait for the child and check exit status.\n        let status = child\n            .wait()\n            .with_context(|| format!(\"failed to wait for hook: {command}\"))?;\n\n        if !status.success() {\n            anyhow::bail!(\n                \"hook exited with status {}: {command}\",\n                status.code().unwrap_or(-1)\n            );\n        }\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// HTTP POST the event JSON to a webhook URL.\n    ///\n    /// Sets `Content-Type: application/json` and applies a 10-second timeout.\n    /// Returns an error if the request fails or the server returns a non-2xx\n    /// status. This is typically done at the beginning of `Worker::run()`.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct Telemetry {\n    worker_id: WorkerId,\n    session_id: String,\n    sequence: Arc<AtomicU64>,\n    /// Wrapped in Arc<Mutex<Option<...>>> so that `shutdown()` can drop the\n    /// sender explicitly (closing the channel) even while clones still exist.\n    sender: Arc<std::sync::Mutex<Option<mpsc::UnboundedSender<TelemetryEvent>>>>,\n    /// Pending writer state that needs to be spawned in an async context.\n    /// This is `Some` until `start()` is called.\n    pending_writer: Arc<std::sync::Mutex<Option<PendingWriter>>>,\n    /// JoinHandle for the background writer task, set by `start()`.\n    writer_handle: Arc<std::sync::Mutex<Option<tokio::task::JoinHandle<()>>>>,\n}\n\n/// Holds the receiver and sinks until they can be spawned in an async context.\nstruct PendingWriter {\n    receiver: mpsc::UnboundedReceiver<TelemetryEvent>,\n    file_sink: Option<FileSink>,\n    stdout_sink: Option<StdoutSink>,\n    hook_sink: Option<HookSink>,\n}\n\nimpl Telemetry {\n    /// Create a telemetry emitter that writes to a `FileSink`.\n    ///\n    /// Does not spawn any async tasks. Call [`start()`](Self::start) from\n    /// within a tokio runtime context before emitting events.\n    pub fn new(worker_id: WorkerId) -> Self {\n        let session_id = generate_session_id();\n        let (sender, receiver) = mpsc::unbounded_channel();\n\n        // Try to create a file sink; fall back to no-op on error.\n        let file_sink: Option<FileSink> = FileSink::new(&worker_id, &session_id)\n            .map_err(|e| {\n                tracing::warn!(error = %e, \"failed to create telemetry file sink\");\n            })\n            .ok();\n\n        let sequence = Arc::new(AtomicU64::new(0));\n        let pending = PendingWriter {\n            receiver,\n            file_sink,\n            stdout_sink: None,\n            hook_sink: None,\n        };\n\n        Telemetry {\n            worker_id,\n            session_id,\n            sequence,\n            sender: Arc::new(std::sync::Mutex::new(Some(sender))),\n            pending_writer: Arc::new(std::sync::Mutex::new(Some(pending))),\n            writer_handle: Arc::new(std::sync::Mutex::new(None)),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Create a telemetry emitter with both file and stdout sinks.\n    ///\n    /// Does not spawn any async tasks. Call [`start()`](Self::start) from\n    /// within a tokio runtime context before emitting events.","numLines":600,"startLine":1088,"totalLines":3701}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01ACSEY3Pj3Nnu1SGcUXndYM","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# NEEDLE Implementation Plan\n2\t\n3\t> **N**avigates **E**very **E**nqueued **D**eliverable, **L**ogs **E**ffort\n4\t\n5\t## Design Principles\n6\t\n7\tThese six principles are non-negotiable. Every design decision in this plan traces back to one or more of them.\n8\t\n9\t1. **Deterministic order.** Given the same queue state, every worker computes the same bead ordering. There is no randomness in selection. Ties are broken by creation time.\n10\t\n11\t2. **Explicit outcome paths.** Every possible result of every operation has a named handler. If an outcome can happen, it has a handler. If it doesn't have a handler, it cannot happen. The type system enforces exhaustiveness.\n12\t\n13\t3. **Platform and model agnostic.** NEEDLE wraps any headless CLI that accepts a prompt and exits. It runs on any POSIX system. It does not depend on any specific AI provider, model, or API.\n14\t\n15\t4. **Observable by default.** Every state transition, claim attempt, dispatch, and outcome emits structured telemetry. A silent worker is a broken worker. Telemetry is structured from origin (JSONL) and exportable as OpenTelemetry (OTLP) so any compliant backend — Tempo, Jaeger, Grafana, Honeycomb, Datadog, FABRIC — can consume NEEDLE's signals without a custom adapter.\n16\t\n17\t5. **Self-healing.** Workers detect and recover from stuck states, stale claims, crashed peers, and corrupted databases without human intervention. Recovery paths are explicit, not heuristic.\n18\t\n19\t6. **Separation of concerns.** The orchestrator does not execute work. The agent does not manage state. The bead store does not enforce workflow. Each component has one job.\n20\t\n21\t---\n22\t\n23\t## Architecture Overview\n24\t\n25\tNEEDLE is composed of five layers:\n26\t\n27\t```\n28\t┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n29\t│                        CLI Layer                              │\n30\t│  needle run | stop | list | attach | status | config          │\n31\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n32\t│                     Worker Layer                              │\n33\t│  Worker loop, strand waterfall, session management            │\n34\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n35\t│                  Coordination Layer                            │\n36\t│   │\n39\t│  Adapter interface, dispatch, result capture                  │\n40\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n41\t│                   Foundation Layer Every design decision in this plan traces back to one or more of them.\n\n1. **Deterministic order.** Given the same queue state, every worker computes the same bead ordering. There is no randomness in selection. Ties are broken by creation time.\n\n2. **Explicit outcome paths.** Every possible result of every operation has a named handler. If an outcome can happen, it has a handler. If it doesn't have a handler, it cannot happen. The type system enforces exhaustiveness.\n\n3. **Platform and model agnostic.** NEEDLE wraps any headless CLI that accepts a prompt and exits. It runs on any POSIX system. It does not depend on any specific AI provider, model, or API.\n\n4. **Observable by default.** Every state transition, claim attempt, dispatch, and outcome emits structured telemetry. A silent worker is a broken worker. Telemetry is structured from origin (JSONL) and exportable as OpenTelemetry (OTLP) so any compliant backend — Tempo, Jaeger, Grafana, Honeycomb, Datadog, FABRIC — can consume NEEDLE's signals without a custom adapter.\n\n5. **Self-healing.** Workers detect and recover from stuck states, stale claims, crashed peers, and corrupted databases without human intervention. Recovery paths are explicit, not heuristic.\n\n6. **Separation of concerns.** The orchestrator does not execute work. The agent does not manage state. The bead store does not enforce workflow. Each component has one job.\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\nNEEDLE is composed of five layers:\n\n```\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                        CLI Layer                              │\n│  needle run | stop | list | attach | status | config          │\n├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                     Worker Layer                              │\n│  Worker loop, strand waterfall, session management            │\n├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                  Coordination Layer                            │\n│  Claiming, locking, heartbeats, peer awareness                │\n├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                    Agent Layer                                 │\n│  Adapter interface, dispatch, result capture                  │\n├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                   Foundation Layer                             │\n│  Telemetry, configuration, bead store interface, self-healing │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Component Map\n\n| Component | Responsibility | Inputs | Outputs |\n|-----------|---------------|--------|---------|\n| **CLI** | Parse commands, manage sessions | User commands | Worker processes |\n| **Worker** | Execute the strand waterfall loop | Bead queue state | Dispatch requests, state transitions |\n| **StrandRunner** | Evaluate strands in sequence | Queue state, config | Next bead or escalation |\n| **Claimer** | Atomic bead claiming with serialization | Candidate bead ID | Claimed bead or race-lost signal |\n| **PromptBuilder** | Construct deterministic prompts from bead context | Claimed bead | Prompt string |\n| **Dispatcher** | Load adapter, render template, execute agent | Prompt, adapter config | Agent process handle |\n| **OutcomeHandler** | Route exit code to explicit handler | Exit code, stdout/stderr | State transition |\n| **Telemetry** | Structured event emission | Any component event | JSONL records |\n| **HealthMonitor** | Heartbeat, stuck detection, peer awareness | Worker state | Recovery actions |\n| **ConfigLoader** | Hierarchical config resolution | Files, env, CLI args | Resolved config |\n| **BeadStore** | Abstract interface to bead backend | CRUD operations | Bead records |\n| **Mitosis** | Split multi-task beads into children with dedup | Failed bead, parent's existing children | Child beads or no-op |\n\n---\n\n## Language Decision\n\nThe implementation language must provide:\n\n| Requirement | Why | Source |\n|-------------|-----|--------|\n| Exhaustive pattern matching | Every outcome must be handled; compiler enforces it | Principle 2, bead-lifecycle-bugs.md |\n| Real module system | 45K single-file bash was unmaintainable | bash-at-scale-problems.md |\n| Structured error types | Silent failures caused cascading bugs | claim-race-conditions.md |\n| Native JSON support | Fragile jq parsing corrupted state | worker-starvation-lessons.md |\n| Proper concurrency primitives | flock/trap/PID files were inadequate | concurrency-approaches-compared.md |\n| Single binary distribution | NEEDLE must be trivially installable | Principle 3 |\n| Cross-platform | Linux, macOS at minimum | Principle 3 |\n| Static analysis | Catch undefined functions, unused variables at compile time | bundler-build-integrity.md |\n\n**Recommended: Rust.** Exhaustive `match`, `Result<T, E>` error handling, `serde_json`, `tokio` for async, single binary via static linking, cross-compilation. The beads ecosystem already has Rust precedent (beads_rust, beads-polis).\n\n**Acceptable alternative: Go.** Simpler learning curve, good concurrency, single binary. Lacks exhaustive matching (requires discipline instead of compiler enforcement).\n\n**Not acceptable: Bash, Python, Node.** Bash failed at scale (documented). {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01HuLcrgMNv6aZNUyK26YaPQ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I have a good understanding of the codebase. Let me analyze what needs to be done:\n\n1. The current `TelemetrySink` trait has:\n   - `write(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> Result<()>`\n   - `flush(&self) -> Result<()>`\n\n2. The task asks for a `Sink` trait with:\n   - `accept(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> Result<()>`\n   - `flush(&self, deadline: Duration) -> Result<()>`\n\n3. The `TelemetryBus` (or `Telemetry` dispatcher) should hold `Vec<Box<dyn Sink>>` instead of specific typed sinks.\n\n\n4. The `flush(deadline)` method will be invoked during graceful shutdown, and I need to migrate `FileSink`, `StdoutSink`, and `HookSink` to implement this new trait while refactoring `PendingWriter` to work with a vector of boxed sinks instead of individual typed fields, with special handling for `HookSink` dispatch failures.\n\nNow I'm realizing the challenge: `HookSink` has unique behavior where failed dispatches emit error events that feed back into the file sink, which breaks the uniform abstraction if everything just implements `Sink`. I think the cleanest approach is to keep `HookSink` special-cased in the writer's fan-out logic while the other sinks follow the standard trait pattern. The challenge is that `HookSink::dispatch` currently returns failure events that get written to the file sink, so if I make `accept` uniform across all sinks, I need to preserve this cross-sink error reporting behavior—either by having `HookSink` handle failures internally through tracing or an internal buffer, or by writing them during flush, while still keeping the tests green. I need to check what the existing tests expect to understand what behavior I'm preserving. The core challenge is that `HookSink` needs to write failure events somewhere, but doing that through the bus creates a circular dependency. I'm considering whether the bus should handle failure routing directly, or if `HookSink` should hold a reference to an inner sink for failures.
